Human-made values by UNSCEAR are from the Japanese National Institute of Radiological Sciences, which summarized the UNSCEAR data.</small></dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effect_on_electronics">Effect on electronics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Effect on electronics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Cosmic rays have sufficient energy to alter the states of circuit components in <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronic</a> <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">integrated circuits</a>, causing transient errors to occur (such as corrupted data in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Random_access_memory" title="Random access memory">electronic memory devices</a> or incorrect performance of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CPU" title="CPU">CPUs</a>) often referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Soft_error" title="Soft error">soft errors</a>." This has been a problem in <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a> at extremely high-altitude, such as in <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellites</a>, but with <a href="/wiki/Transistor" title="Transistor">transistors</a> becoming smaller and smaller, this is becoming an increasing concern in ground-level electronics as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Studies by <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> in the 1990s suggest that computers typically experience about one cosmic-ray-induced error per 256 megabytes of <a href="/wiki/Random-access_memory" title="Random-access memory">RAM</a> per month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> To alleviate this problem, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intel_Corporation" title="Intel Corporation">Intel Corporation</a> has proposed a cosmic ray detector that could be integrated into future high-density <a href="/wiki/Microprocessor" title="Microprocessor">microprocessors</a>, allowing the processor to repeat the last command following a cosmic-ray event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2008, data corruption in a flight control system caused an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">Airbus A330</a> airliner to twice <a href="/wiki/Qantas_Flight_72" title="Qantas Flight 72">plunge hundreds of feet</a>, resulting in injuries to multiple passengers and crew members. Cosmic rays were investigated among other possible causes of the data corruption, but were ultimately ruled out as being very unlikely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Radiation_hardening" title="Radiation hardening">Radiation hardening</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Significance_to_aerospace_travel">Significance to aerospace travel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Significance to aerospace travel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_threat_from_cosmic_rays" title="Health threat from cosmic rays">Health threat from cosmic rays</a></div>\n<p>Galactic cosmic rays are one of the most important barriers standing in the way of plans for interplanetary travel by crewed spacecraft. Cosmic rays also pose a threat to electronics placed aboard outgoing probes. In 2010, a malfunction aboard the <a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a> space probe was credited to a single flipped bit, probably caused by a cosmic ray. Strategies such as physical or magnetic shielding for spacecraft have been considered in order to minimize the damage to electronics and human beings caused by cosmic rays.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-globus-2002_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-globus-2002-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atkinson-2005_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-atkinson-2005-92">[92]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1017" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png/250px-PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png/375px-PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png/500px-PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Comparison of radiation doses, including the amount detected on the trip from Earth to Mars by the <a href="/wiki/Radiation_assessment_detector" title="Radiation assessment detector">RAD</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">MSL</a> (2011 &#8211; 2013).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20130531a_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-SCI-20130531a-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20130531b_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-SCI-20130531b-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20130530_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20130530-24">[24]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Flying 12 kilometres (39,000&#160;ft) high, passengers and crews of <a href="/wiki/Jet_airliner" title="Jet airliner">jet airliners</a> are exposed to at least 10 times the cosmic ray dose that people at <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a> receive. Aircraft flying <a href="/wiki/Polar_route" title="Polar route">polar routes</a> near the <a href="/wiki/Geomagnetic_pole" title="Geomagnetic pole">geomagnetic poles</a> are at particular risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Role_in_lightning">Role in lightning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Role in lightning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Cosmic rays have been implicated in the triggering of electrical breakdown in <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">lightning</a>. It has been proposed that essentially all lightning is triggered through a relativistic process, "<a href="/wiki/Runaway_breakdown" title="Runaway breakdown">runaway breakdown</a>", seeded by cosmic ray secondaries. Subsequent development of the lightning discharge then occurs through "conventional breakdown" mechanisms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Postulated_role_in_climate_change">Postulated role in climate change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Postulated role in climate change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A role for cosmic rays in climate was suggested by <a href="/wiki/Edward_P._Ney" title="Edward P. Ney">Edward P. Ney</a> in 1959<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NATURE_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-NATURE-97">[97]</a></sup> and by <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Dickinson" title="Robert E. Dickinson">Robert E. Dickinson</a> in 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dickinson-1975_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-dickinson-1975-98">[98]</a></sup> It has been postulated that cosmic rays may have been responsible for major climatic change and mass-extinction in the past. According to Adrian Mellott and Mikhail Medvedev, 62-million-year cycles in biological marine populations correlate with the motion of the Earth relative to the galactic plane and increases in exposure to cosmic rays.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The researchers suggest that this and <a href="/wiki/Gamma_ray" title="Gamma ray">gamma ray</a> bombardments deriving from local <a href="/wiki/Supernova" title="Supernova">supernovae</a> could have affected <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mutation_rate" title="Mutation rate">mutation rates</a>, and might be linked to decisive alterations in the Earth\'s climate, and to the <a href="/wiki/Extinction_event" title="Extinction event">mass-extinctions</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ordovician" title="Ordovician">Ordovician</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Danish physicist <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Svensmark" title="Henrik Svensmark">Henrik Svensmark</a> has controversially argued that because <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_variation" title="Solar variation">solar variation</a> modulates the cosmic ray flux on Earth, they would consequently affect the rate of cloud formation and hence be an indirect cause of <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Svensmark is one of several scientists <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_scientists_opposing_the_mainstream_scientific_assessment_of_global_warming" title="List of scientists opposing the mainstream scientific assessment of global warming">outspokenly opposed to the mainstream scientific assessment of global warming</a>, leading to concerns that the proposition that cosmic rays are connected to global warming could be ideologically biased rather than scientifically based.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup>  Other scientists have vigorously criticized Svensmark for sloppy and inconsistent work: one example is adjustment of cloud data that understates error in lower cloud data, but not in high cloud data;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> another example is "incorrect handling of the physical data" resulting in graphs that do not show the correlations they claim to show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Despite Svensmark\'s assertions, galactic cosmic rays have shown no statistically significant influence on changes in cloud cover,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> and demonstrated to have no causal relationship to changes in global temperature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_mass_extinction_factor">Possible mass extinction factor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Possible mass extinction factor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A handful of studies conclude that a nearby supernova or series of supernovas caused the <a href="/wiki/Pliocene" title="Pliocene">Pliocene</a> marine megafauna extinction event by substantially increasing radiation levels to hazardous amounts for large seafaring animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_and_experiments">Research and experiments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Research and experiments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cosmic-ray_observatory" title="Cosmic-ray observatory">Cosmic-ray observatory</a></div>\n<p>There are a number of cosmic-ray research initiatives, listed below.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground-based">Ground-based</span><span
